<div id="review_1506235805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506235805" />
    <a title="Brittney Clark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51062303-brittney-clark"><img alt="Brittney Clark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601937377p2/51062303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1506235805?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney Clark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney Clark" href="/user/show/51062303-brittney-clark">Brittney Clark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1506235805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13955182282459024032">In the memoir Death Be Not Proud, John Gunther tells a story of his son Johnny Gunther after he has been diagnosed with brain cancer. Gunther tells Johnny’s life story before he was diagnosed with brain cancer all the way through Johnny’s last days as a cancer patient. As the reader begins the book they learn that Johnny was one of the most extraordinary people you would ever meet. Johnny was only seventeen when he passed on June 30, 1947. Gunther, already being a journalist takes you on a journ</span>
  <span id="freeText13955182282459024032" style="display:none">In the memoir Death Be Not Proud, John Gunther tells a story of his son Johnny Gunther after he has been diagnosed with brain cancer. Gunther tells Johnny’s life story before he was diagnosed with brain cancer all the way through Johnny’s last days as a cancer patient. As the reader begins the book they learn that Johnny was one of the most extraordinary people you would ever meet. Johnny was only seventeen when he passed on June 30, 1947. Gunther, already being a journalist takes you on a journey throughout Johnny’s life and little by little you learn everything he loved in life and how he dealt with his cancer at such a young age.<br />	The book was very heartfelt and made you feel as if you were right there next to Johnny as he battled his cancer. What I very much liked about this book is how John Gunther talks about his son. The way he writes you can tell he loved his son very much and was so proud of what all he had accomplished at such a young age. At some points of the book when Johnny started to get better you almost believed there would be a happy ending even if you already knew that he eventually was not going to make it. The book actually made me cry. Of all the books I have read very few have made me cry and this book was one of them. It was a very emotional yet depressing book. In my opinion the funeral scene was very well written and I like the way Gunther made you feel as if you could see Johnny there as he laid in his coffin.<br />	Every positive side always has a negative but with this book there were very few. There were only a couple of things I did not like in this book. One part of the book I did not like is when Gunther would start telling you every single detail and even give you a list of what medications Johnny took that day or what he ate throughout the entire day. Sometimes that much detail made it hard to even turn to the next page, but fortunately he would go into every detail a couple of times he would not do it very often. I feel as if the book lacked some of John Gunther’s emotions. I understand this memoir was about Johnny but I did wonder quite often how he was feeling on the days Johnny was getting worse and how he was feeling while he looked at his son struggling with his brain cancer.<br />	My overall rating for this book is a four stars because Gunther did an amazing job of telling Johnny’s journey but parts of the book would get quite boring. I would say about 85% of the book is interesting but 15% is the boring part of this memoir. Do not get me wrong this book is a very great book because it takes you on such an emotional roller coaster from when Johnny was first diagnosed to his best days during his cancer journey. I do wish I could have met Johnny he did sound like an incredible young boy and I wish he could have lived longer without any pain.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13955182282459024032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_906621002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906621002" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37400-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1176051726p2/37400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906621002?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/37400-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906621002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15851209307121093225">I grabbed this book off my shelf several times over the past couple years but always put it back out of the fear that it would be all too depressing. As a father myself, it sounded like a rather unpleasant experience to read another father chronicle the death of his seventeen-year-old son. But when I finally put those concerns aside, I found that <i>Death Be Not Proud</i> wasn't all that depressing after all. But it also wasn't very good. <br/><br/>The book offered very little for me in terms of reflections on l</span>
  <span id="freeText15851209307121093225" style="display:none">I grabbed this book off my shelf several times over the past couple years but always put it back out of the fear that it would be all too depressing. As a father myself, it sounded like a rather unpleasant experience to read another father chronicle the death of his seventeen-year-old son. But when I finally put those concerns aside, I found that <i>Death Be Not Proud</i> wasn't all that depressing after all. But it also wasn't very good. <br /><br />The book offered very little for me in terms of reflections on life and death. Gunther's telling focused primarily on the physical aspects of his son's tumor and treatment, and didn't delve too deeply into the emotions of losing a child. <br /><br />In some ways this isn't terribly surprising. Gunther, along with his ex-wife, were after all the type of parents who shipped their child off to a boarding school and even in the midst of his fatal illness seemed to be more concerned about their own lives than remaining by their dying son's side. The father continued to travel for his work, both parents took vacations while their son was in the hospital, and rather tellingly Johnny was the one to phone his parents every morning and evening. <br /><br />I get that over a 15-month ordeal that the parents wouldn't be by Johnny's side at every minute, but jaunting off on holiday at a time when your kid could die any minute is something I can't imagine doing. Obviously no one knows how they would react until they were in such a horrible situation, but I would like to think that if it were my child I would have prioritized being with him every possible minute while I still had him.<br /><br />It wasn't until the very end of the book when Frances Gunther interjected her own few pages that some real emotion shone through. Yes, John Gunther was clearly proud of his son and I'm sure he was a good father when he was around but <i>Death Be Not Proud</i> left me with the feeling that its writing was more about John than Johnny. That's a shame because it is clear through his father's telling that Johnny was a bright, upbeat kid who bravely faced his meeting with death. But most of the emotional impact of that 15-month ordeal was stripped bare in the elder Gunther's overly-clinical telling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15851209307121093225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17445940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17445940" />
    <a title="Susanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/304545-susanna"><img alt="Susanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187890152p2/304545.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17445940?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanna" href="/user/show/304545-susanna">Susanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17445940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17244549210315887351">Somehow, I keep being drawn to books on death.<br/><br/>This one very dissimilar to my own grief, as it is about the death of a child (17 yrs). Nonetheless it impressed me in various things.<br/>- Gunther himself says at the end that "the whys and wherefores of the celestial bookkeeping involved... I will not go into here." They are presented as an agnostic family. Rather he states that "the central pith and substance of what I am trying to write" is "that it was his spirit ... that kept him invincibly alive a</span>
  <span id="freeText17244549210315887351" style="display:none">Somehow, I keep being drawn to books on death.<br /><br />This one very dissimilar to my own grief, as it is about the death of a child (17 yrs). Nonetheless it impressed me in various things.<br />- Gunther himself says at the end that "the whys and wherefores of the celestial bookkeeping involved... I will not go into here." They are presented as an agnostic family. Rather he states that "the central pith and substance of what I am trying to write" is "that it was his spirit ... that kept him invincibly alive against such dreadful obstacles for so long." This is making me think. On the one hand it sounds very humanist to say its all about our will to live, yet I accept there is a truth there, being as a do believe that the sheer force of our will and mind and attitude is so powerful in our physical health -- and yet even this is God's grace. There is no denying that I would like to exhibit the same fight and dignity as this victim of a brain tumour should I ever have to face the same.<br />- His mom writes a few pages at the end that are truly beautiful. I have taken her admonition and fierce truthfulness to heart: "Today, when I see parents impatient or tired or bored with their children, I wish I could say to them, But they are alive, think of the wonder of that! They may be a care and a burden, but think, they are alive! You can touch them -- what a miracle! You don't have to hold back sudden tears when you see just a headline about the Yale-Harvard game because you know your boy will never see the Yale-Harvard game, never see the house in Paris he was born in, never bring ome his girl, and you will not hand down your jewels to his bride and will have no grandchildren to play with and spoil. Your sons and daughters live. Think of that-- not dead but alive! Exult and sing."<br />- Interesting to read about how tumours were treated in 1946. I have a scary feeling in 50 years we will read about chemotherapy with the same shock and horror. (Oh, guess the one thing that works for a while ... yes, that's right, a radical diet!)<br /><br />Just for the record (again), I miss my mama.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17244549210315887351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1063677881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063677881" />
    <a title="Jhastings09" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35141898-jhastings09"><img alt="Jhastings09" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411997981p2/35141898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063677881?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jhastings09" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jhastings09" href="/user/show/35141898-jhastings09">Jhastings09</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35141898-jhastings09?shelf=biog-autob-memoir">biog-autob-memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063677881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11757020101503788909"> <i>Death Be Not Proud</i> is a non-fiction book about a high schooler named Jonny Gunther that was diagnosed with a brain tumor. It began when Johnny got a stiff neck but very quickly turned into a giant brain tumor. During his year and a half battle with a brain tumor Johnny managed to graduate high school, and even better, get accepted into college at Harvard University. But these accomplishments of his were only short lived, as Johnny died a few days after receiving this news. <br/><br/> I think <i>Death Be Not</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11757020101503788909" style="display:none"> <i>Death Be Not Proud</i> is a non-fiction book about a high schooler named Jonny Gunther that was diagnosed with a brain tumor. It began when Johnny got a stiff neck but very quickly turned into a giant brain tumor. During his year and a half battle with a brain tumor Johnny managed to graduate high school, and even better, get accepted into college at Harvard University. But these accomplishments of his were only short lived, as Johnny died a few days after receiving this news. <br /><br /> I think <i>Death Be Not Proud</i> is the first memoir that I have ever read, and reading non-fiction books is hard for me. Which is why I thought I should read it. What makes non-fiction hard for me to read is that it always tells a true story. As easy as it seems I always end up forgetting that what I'm reading actually happened. Due to this, I normally think that some miracle is gonna happen and everyone will be safe, but then I turn the page to realize that this miracle could never happen. I think that people need to read more non-fiction because non-fiction books are what grounds us to reality. Although non-fiction books aren't as action packed as fictional books, they can still catch your eye. Whether it's a happy theme or a terrible gruesome themed book, true stories always seem to make me think about, <i>if this were to happen to me, what would I do?</i> Another thing about non-fiction is that there's always something from the book that sticks with you forever. This line right here is what I'll never forget about <i>Death Be Not Proud</i>. <br /><br /> <i>What is life? It departs covertly. Like a thief Death took him. (Gunther 137)</i><br /><br /> This line captured the early death of a child and really made me think about what life actually is. It made me look into the book and ask questions about life. Like why is life so fragile? Although I liked this book a lot, it wasn't amazing which is why I'm give this book a<b> 7 out of 10</b>. <br /><br /> <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11757020101503788909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_267220265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267220265" />
    <a title="Sierra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6178431-sierra"><img alt="Sierra" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267220265?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sierra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sierra" href="/user/show/6178431-sierra">Sierra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267220265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1462079704477072207"><u> Death Be not Proud </u> by John Gunther is a memoir about his son Johnny's sickness. Johnny is a seventeen year old boy who is diagnosed with a brain tumor. Johnny is sent to see Tracy Putnam a neurologist by his family doctor Traeger.Johnny has his first operation on April 29 which last six hours. Johnny had a welt on his head the size of a grape fruit. after his first operation Johnny see's countless doctor and tries many varieties of treatment. He tried mustard gas, a special diet, another opera</span>
  <span id="freeText1462079704477072207" style="display:none"><u> Death Be not Proud </u> by John Gunther is a memoir about his son Johnny's sickness. Johnny is a seventeen year old boy who is diagnosed with a brain tumor. Johnny is sent to see Tracy Putnam a neurologist by his family doctor Traeger.Johnny has his first operation on April 29 which last six hours. Johnny had a welt on his head the size of a grape fruit. after his first operation Johnny see's countless doctor and tries many varieties of treatment. He tried mustard gas, a special diet, another operation, etc. Through out it all Johnny stayed completely selfless and didn't complain at all. Johnny was a very intelligent and sensitive boy. His mother was one of his best friend and he talked about everything with her. With his father he is more formal but still is close. During the summer Johnny does experiments and tries to act normal. During his fifteen month sickness Johnny spend months in the hospital off and on. In this time he also manged to catch up with school work , graduate high school and take college entrance exams for Harvard.He got to walk across the stage with the rest of his class. Through out this Johnny remained happy. He suffered in silence; he knew he was dying. His parents tried to sugar coat it, and he pretended to believe them. Johnny died June 30,1947. He passed in his sleep and had no pain. This book takes place in the 1940's in the New England part of the U.S. This is significant because if it was set present day more could have been done with the newer technology.The tone of this novel was of sadness. This quote shows that: "My grief, I find, is not desolation or rebellion at universal law or deity. I find grief to be much simpler and sadder... All the things he loved tear at my heart because he is no longer here on earth to enjoy them. All the things he loved!" I loved this book it made me cry multiple times. I thought it was amazing , I recommend it to everyone! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1462079704477072207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1058952667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058952667" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35141888-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058952667?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/35141888-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35141888-lauren?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35141888-lauren?shelf=most-challenging">most-challenging</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058952667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer961260333556816737"> This book was my first Non-Fiction book I have read all year, or possibly in my whole life, and I couldn’t be more thankful that I chose it as ‘my first’. After the first few pages, it was clear to me that I hadn’t read anything quite like it. It’s obvious that the wording is different, but that is understandable once recognizing the time period. But the book was so different because the way John Gunther writes is indescribable. He writes with such little emotion, but yet when it comes to the s</span>
  <span id="freeText961260333556816737" style="display:none"> This book was my first Non-Fiction book I have read all year, or possibly in my whole life, and I couldn’t be more thankful that I chose it as ‘my first’. After the first few pages, it was clear to me that I hadn’t read anything quite like it. It’s obvious that the wording is different, but that is understandable once recognizing the time period. But the book was so different because the way John Gunther writes is indescribable. He writes with such little emotion, but yet when it comes to the sullen, sad moments, you can almost hear the crack in his voice and see the water welling in his eyes. Differentiating between the happy and the sad moments is probably the hardest part about reading this book. John Gunther describes the sad moments in some what the same matter as he describes the happy moments, which could possibly be influenced by the fact that he is writing about his son’s death. But by leaving the moments open for our own perspective, Gunther lets us imagine ourselves in a similar situation, making the predicament more relatable to us as the readers.<br /><br /> The way John Gunther writes this piece is interesting and intriguing. He doesn’t dwell on any event or topic long. His writing is bold and moving, yet calm and quiet. He makes us feel furious about the situation but also hopeful, that something as horrible as this would never happen to someone like Johnny. The pace of the book is slow, but I believe this adds to the piece. It gives Gunther time to explain his writing and also gives us time to comprehend everything we are soaking in. If he were to write this novel fast and quick paced, I believe it would have lost all its significant meaning and purpose. Therefore, John Gunther does an excellent job on this piece and I don’t believe that there is anything I would change about this book. I give Death Be Not Proud a 3.5 out of 5 star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="961260333556816737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TEFTQ7ZsujGrl7LayDIfW68fk6btsWy5PtNvGZYR6bFRdGzODT7cHji/6GdjmD34UDT/A3Q1Xm0qv3Eh3Yb3mQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

DeVit<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4694497861828803247\" style=\"display:none\">Cancer touches everybody’s life in one way or another. But most of us know very little about how the disease works, why we treat it the way we do, and the personalities whose dedication got us where we are today. For fifty years, Dr. Vincent T. DeVita Jr. has been one of those key players: he has held just about every major position in the field, and he developed the first successful chemotherapy treatment for Hodgkin’s lymphoma, a breakthrough the American Society of Clinical Oncologists has called the top research advance in half a century of chemotherapy. As one of oncology’s leading figures, DeVita knows what cancer looks like from the lab bench and the bedside. The Death of Cancer is his illuminating and deeply personal look at the science and the history of one of the world’s most formidable diseases. In DeVita’s hands, even the most complex medical concepts are comprehensible.\n\nCowritten with DeVita’s daughter, the science writer Elizabeth DeVita-Raeburn, The Death of Cancer is also a personal tale about the false starts and major breakthroughs, the strong-willed oncologists who clashed with conservative administrators (and one another), and the courageous patients whose willingness to test cutting-edge research helped those oncologists find potential treatments. An emotionally compelling and informative read, The Death of Cancer is also a call to arms. DeVita believes that we’re well on our way to curing cancer but that there are things we need to change in order to get there. Mortality rates are declining, but America’s cancer patients are still being shortchanged—by timid doctors, by misguided national agendas, by compromised bureaucracies, and by a lack of access to information about the strengths and weaknesses of the nation’s cancer centers.\n\nWith historical depth and authenticity, DeVita reveals the true story of the fight against cancer.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/68809.John_Gunther">About John Gunther</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/68809.John_Gunther"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235985796p3/68809.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/68809.John_Gunther">John Gunther
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
82
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17347308086520945143">John Gunther was one of the best known and most admired journalists of his day, and his series of "Inside" books, starting with <i>Inside Europe</i> in 1936, were immensely popular profiles of the major world powers. One critic noted that it was Gunther's special gift to "unite the best qualities of the newspaperman and the historian." It was a gift that readers responded to enthusiastically. The "Inside</span>
  <span id="freeText17347308086520945143" style="display:none">John Gunther was one of the best known and most admired journalists of his day, and his series of "Inside" books, starting with <i>Inside Europe</i> in 1936, were immensely popular profiles of the major world powers. One critic noted that it was Gunther's special gift to "unite the best qualities of the newspaperman and the historian." It was a gift that readers responded to enthusiastically. The "Inside" books sold 3,500,000 copies over a period of thirty years.<br /><br />While publicly a bon vivant and modest celebrity, Gunther in his private life suffered disappointment and tragedy. He and Frances Fineman, whom he married in 1927, had a daughter who died four months after her birth in 1929. The Gunthers divorced in 1944. In 1947, their beloved son Johnny died after a long, heartbreaking fight with brain cancer. Gunther wrote his classic memoir <i>Death Be Not Proud</i>, published in 1949, to commemorate the courage and spirit of this extraordinary boy. Gunther remarried in 1948, and he and his second wife, Jane Perry Vandercook, adopted a son.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17347308086520945143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
